## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / concentration-time ODE models)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of a chemical concentration A(t), which is the standard formulation of reaction kinetics via rate laws. With only {t, A} available, common models express dA_dt as an A-dependent rate (reaction order, saturation/inhibition) possibly modulated by explicit time-dependence (changing conditions, catalyst deactivation, forcing).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate depletion when reactant is in excess or surface-limited)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay; many elementary decompositions)
- Second-order (self-reaction): dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular with identical reactants or overall second-order lumped behavior)
- General n-th order: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical overall order / power-law kinetics)
- First-order with source term: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A (net production/decay with background generation or feed; sign determined by fit)
- Relaxation to equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (approach to steady concentration c1; linearized reversible/relaxation behavior)
- Autocatalytic / self-accelerating then depletion: dA_dt = c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (growth at low A with nonlinear self-limitation; common in autocatalysis approximations)
- Rational inhibition (self-inhibited rate): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A) (rate increases ~A at low A and saturates at high A due to inhibition/crowding)
- Time-varying rate constant (linear drift): dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * t) * A (slowly changing conditions, e.g., temperature/programmed ramp approximated linearly in time)
- Exponentially decaying activity (catalyst deactivation / light decay): dA_dt = -c0 * A * exp(-c1 * t) (effective rate constant decreases over time)
- Stretched-exponential time modulation: dA_dt = -c0 * A * exp(-c1 * t**c2) (broad distribution of deactivation times / non-single-exponential aging)
- Periodic forcing of kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) (modulated irradiation, mixing cycles, or other periodic external control)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Sign constraint for depletion-only systems: if A is being consumed without feed, expect dA_dt <= 0 for A > 0, often implemented by an overall negative factor multiplying a nonnegative function of A.
- Reaction order identification: log(-dA_dt) linear in log(A) suggests power-law form dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1, where c1 is the apparent order.
- Near-equilibrium linearization: if trajectories approach a steady level, dA_dt often factors as -(A - c_eq) times a positive rate, yielding exponential relaxation when the rate is roughly constant.
- Autocatalysis signature: dA_dt positive at small A but negative at large A indicates competing +A and -A**2 terms (or higher-order inhibition).
- Saturation/inhibition behavior: when |dA_dt| increases with A initially but plateaus, rational forms like A/(1 + c*A) or other bounded-in-A kinetics are typical.
- Time-dependent conditions: systematic drift in rates at fixed A suggests explicit t-dependence in an effective rate constant, e.g., k(t) = c0 + c1*t or k(t) = c0*exp(-c1*t).
- Positivity preservation: physically valid kinetics typically keep A(t) >= 0; models with factors of A (e.g., dA_dt ŌłØ A) naturally prevent crossing below zero.
- Stiffness indicator: very rapid initial changes followed by slow tails often imply multiple time scales, approximated by time-modulated rates or mixed terms (e.g., -c0*A - c1*A**2).

GT Equivalence Verification (CRK3)
============================================================
GT: -c0*A**c1 - c2*A*exp(-c3*_s*t) + c4*_w*cos(log(A + c5))
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.5475*A┬▓ - 0.5475*A*exp(-0.0371*t) + 0.7049*cos(log(A + 1))`

The GT has three distinct basis functions:
1. `A┬▓` (polynomial)
2. `A*exp(╬▒t)` (exponential decay times A)
3. `cos(log(A + 1))` (cosine of logarithm)

The key challenge is the `cos(log(A+1))` term. This is a very specific transcendental function that cannot be represented by polynomials, rational functions, exponentials, or simple trigonometric functions of A.

Let me analyze each candidate for the presence of this basis function:

**Candidates 1-5:** Contain `log(A*c8 + 1)` but NOT `cos(log(...))`. The `log` function alone cannot equal `cos(log(...))`.

**Candidates 6-16:** Contain combinations of polynomials, exponentials, rational functions, `1/Abs(A)`, `t^(1/3)`, etc. None contain `cos(log(...))`.

**Candidates 17-26:** Contain `A^c*exp(t)` terms, rational functions `A/(A+c)`, but no `cos(log(...))`.

**Candidate 27-29:** Rational functions and exponentials, no `cos(log(...))`.

**Candidate 30:** `A┬▓*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3 + c4*exp(c5*t)*sin(c6*t + c7)` - Has `sin` of `t`, not of `log(A+1)`. No match.

**Candidates 31-41:** Polynomials, exponentials, rational functions, `log(A+1)` (not inside cos). No `cos(log(...))`.

**Candidate 42:** `A*c0 + A + A/(A+c1) + A^c2*c3*exp(c4*t) + c5*sin(A*c6 + c7)` - Has `sin(A*c6 + c7)`, not `cos(log(A+1))`. These are fundamentally different functions.

**Candidate 43:** `A*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + A*c3*exp(c4*t)*cos(c5*t) + c6*sin(A*c7 + c8) + c9` - Has `sin(A*c7+c8)` and `cos(c5*t)`, but not `cos(log(A+1))`.

**Candidates 44-50:** Polynomials, exponentials, rational functions. None contain `cos(log(...))`.

**Key conclusion:** The GT contains `cos(log(A+1))`, which is a unique transcendental function. None of the candidates contain this basis function. By the principle of linear independence of basis functions, no combination of the basis functions present in any candidate (polynomials, exponentials, rational functions, `log`, `sin(A)`, `sin(t)`, `cos(t)`, `t^(1/3)`, `1/|A|`, `|A|`) can exactly equal `cos(log(A+1))` for all values of A.
